### File: `src\watcher.rs`

- Size: 12673 bytes
- Modified: SystemTime { intervals: 134182950087420774 }

```rust
   1 | use crate::error::{FlashError, Result};
   2 | use crate::indexer::IndexManager;
   3 | use crate::metadata::MetadataDb;
   4 | use crate::parsers::parse_file;
   5 | use blake3;
   6 | use notify::{Event, EventKind, RecommendedWatcher, RecursiveMode, Watcher};
   7 | use std::collections::HashMap;
   8 | use std::path::{Path, PathBuf};
   9 | use std::sync::{Arc, Mutex};
  10 | use std::time::Duration;
  11 | use tokio::sync::mpsc;
  12 | use tracing::{error, info, warn};
  13 | 
  14 | #[derive(Debug, Clone, Copy, PartialEq, Eq)]
  15 | pub enum WatcherAction {
  16 |     Index,
  17 |     Remove,
  18 | }
  19 | 
  20 | /// Manages active file system watching with debouncing
  21 | pub struct WatcherManager {
  22 |     watchers: HashMap<String, RecommendedWatcher>,
  23 |     _indexer: Arc<IndexManager>,
  24 |     _metadata_db: Arc<MetadataDb>,
  25 |     _runtime_handle: tokio::runtime::Handle,
  26 |     external_tx: mpsc::Sender<(PathBuf, WatcherAction)>,
  27 | }
  28 | 
  29 | impl WatcherManager {
  30 |     pub fn new(
  31 |         indexer: Arc<IndexManager>,
  32 |         metadata_db: Arc<MetadataDb>,
  33 |         allowed_extensions: std::collections::HashSet<String>,
  34 |     ) -> Self {
  35 |         let buffer: Arc<Mutex<HashMap<PathBuf, WatcherAction>>> =
  36 |             Arc::new(Mutex::new(HashMap::new()));
  37 |         let buffer_for_task = buffer.clone();
  38 |         let indexer_for_task = indexer.clone();
  39 |         let metadata_db_for_task = metadata_db.clone();
  40 |         let (external_tx, mut external_rx) = mpsc::channel::<(PathBuf, WatcherAction)>(1000);
  41 |         let runtime_handle = tokio::runtime::Handle::current();
  42 | 
  43 |         // Spawn background processor for debounced events
  44 |         runtime_handle.spawn(async move {
  45 |             loop {
  46 |                 // Use select to handle both periodic flushes and incoming external events
  47 |                 tokio::select! {
  48 |                     res = external_rx.recv() => {
  49 |                         if let Some((path, action)) = res {
  50 |                             if let Ok(mut guard) = buffer_for_task.lock() {
  51 |                                 guard.insert(path, action);
  52 |                             }
  53 |                         }
  54 |                     }
  55 |                     _ = tokio::time::sleep(Duration::from_millis(1000)) => {
  56 |                         let events = {
  57 |                             let mut guard = match buffer_for_task.lock() {
  58 |                                 Ok(g) => g,
  59 |                                 Err(e) => {
  60 |                                     error!("Watcher lock poisoned: {}", e);
  61 |                                     continue;
  62 |                                 }
  63 |                             };
  64 |                             if guard.is_empty() {
  65 |                                 continue;
  66 |                             }
  67 |                             // Take all events
  68 |                             std::mem::take(&mut *guard)
  69 |                         };
  70 | 
  71 |                         let mut needs_commit = false;
  72 | 
  73 |                         // First pass: collect all paths that need to be removed
  74 |                         let remove_paths: Vec<PathBuf> = events
  75 |                             .iter()
  76 |                             .filter(|(_, action)| matches!(action, WatcherAction::Remove))
  77 |                             .map(|(path, _)| path.clone())
  78 |                             .collect();
  79 | 
  80 |                         // Second pass: collect all paths that need to be indexed
  81 |                         let index_paths: Vec<PathBuf> = events
  82 |                             .iter()
  83 |                             .filter(|(_, action)| matches!(action, WatcherAction::Index))
  84 |                             .map(|(path, _)| path.clone())
  85 |                             .collect();
  86 | 
  87 |                         // Process removes first
  88 |                         for path in remove_paths {
  89 |                             let path_str = path.to_string_lossy();
  90 |                             let _ = indexer_for_task.remove_document(&path_str);
  91 |                             match metadata_db_for_task.remove_file(&path) {
  92 |                                 Ok(true) => {
  93 |                                     needs_commit = true;
  94 |                                     info!("Removed file (watcher): {:?}", path);
  95 |                                 }
  96 |                                 Err(e) => error!("Watcher error removing {:?}: {}", path, e),
  97 |                                 _ => {}
  98 |                             }
  99 |                         }
 100 | 
 101 |                         // Then process indexes
 102 |                         let mut docs_to_add = Vec::new();
 103 |                         let mut meta_to_update = Vec::new();
 104 | 
 105 |                         for path in index_paths {
 106 |                             if let Some(ext) = path.extension().and_then(|e| e.to_str()) {
 107 |                                 if !allowed_extensions.contains(&ext.to_lowercase()) {
 108 |                                     continue;
 109 |                                 }
 110 |                             } else {
 111 |                                 continue;
 112 |                             }
 113 | 
 114 |                             match Self::reindex_single_file(&path, &metadata_db_for_task).await {
 115 |                                 Ok(Some((doc, modified, size, hash))) => {
 116 |                                     meta_to_update.push((doc.path.clone(), modified, size, hash));
 117 |                                     docs_to_add.push((doc, modified, size));
 118 |                                 }
 119 |                                 Ok(None) => {} // Skipped or does not exist
 120 |                                 Err(e) => {
 121 |                                     error!("Watcher error indexing {:?}: {}", path, e);
 122 |                                 }
 123 |                             }
 124 |                         }
 125 | 
 126 |                         if !docs_to_add.is_empty() {
 127 |                             if let Err(e) = indexer_for_task.add_documents_batch(&docs_to_add) {
 128 |                                 error!("Watcher error batch adding to index: {}", e);
 129 |                             }
 130 |                             if let Err(e) = metadata_db_for_task.batch_update_metadata(&meta_to_update) {
 131 |                                 error!("Watcher error batch updating DB: {}", e);
 132 |                             } else {
 133 |                                 info!("Re-indexed {} files (watcher)", docs_to_add.len());
 134 |                             }
 135 |                             needs_commit = true;
 136 |                         }
 137 | 
 138 |                         if needs_commit {
 139 |                             if let Err(e) = indexer_for_task.commit() {
 140 |                                 error!("Watcher failed to commit index: {}", e);
 141 |                             } else {
 142 |                                 indexer_for_task.invalidate_cache();
 143 |                                 info!("Watcher committed changes");
 144 |                             }
 145 |                         }
 146 |                     }
 147 |                 }
 148 |             }
 149 |         });
 150 | 
 151 |         Self {
 152 |             watchers: HashMap::new(),
 153 |             _indexer: indexer,
 154 |             _metadata_db: metadata_db,
 155 |             _runtime_handle: runtime_handle,
 156 |             external_tx,
 157 |         }
 158 |     }
 159 | 
 160 |     /// Get a sender to push external events (like USN Journal) into the watcher
 161 |     pub fn event_tx(&self) -> mpsc::Sender<(PathBuf, WatcherAction)> {
 162 |         self.external_tx.clone()
 163 |     }
 164 | 
 165 |     /// Update the list of watched directories
 166 |     pub fn update_watch_list(&mut self, dirs: Vec<String>) -> Result<()> {
 167 |         let current_dirs: std::collections::HashSet<String> = dirs.iter().cloned().collect();
 168 |         let existing_dirs: std::collections::HashSet<String> =
 169 |             self.watchers.keys().cloned().collect();
 170 | 
 171 |         // Remove watchers for directories no longer in the list
 172 |         for dir in existing_dirs.difference(&current_dirs) {
 173 |             self.watchers.remove(dir);
 174 |         }
 175 | 
 176 |         // Add watchers for new directories
 177 |         for dir in current_dirs.difference(&existing_dirs) {
 178 |             let tx = self.external_tx.clone();
 179 |             let mut watcher = notify::recommended_watcher(move |res: notify::Result<Event>| {
 180 |                 if let Ok(event) = res {
 181 |                     match event.kind {
 182 |                         EventKind::Modify(_) | EventKind::Create(_) | EventKind::Remove(_) => {
 183 |                             for path in &event.paths {
 184 |                                 let action = match event.kind {
 185 |                                     EventKind::Remove(_) => WatcherAction::Remove,
 186 |                                     _ => WatcherAction::Index,
 187 |                                 };
 188 |                                 let _ = tx.try_send((path.clone(), action));
 189 |                             }
 190 |                         }
 191 |                         _ => {}
 192 |                     }
 193 |                 }
 194 |             })
 195 |             .map_err(|e| FlashError::Io(std::io::Error::other(e)))?;
 196 | 
 197 |             let path = Path::new(dir);
 198 |             if path.exists() {
 199 |                 watcher
 200 |                     .watch(path, RecursiveMode::Recursive)
 201 |                     .map_err(|e| FlashError::Io(std::io::Error::other(e)))?;
 202 |                 self.watchers.insert(dir.clone(), watcher);
 203 |             }
 204 |         }
 205 | 
 206 |         Ok(())
 207 |     }
 208 | 
 209 |     // Returns parsed document data if file needs re-indexing
 210 |     async fn reindex_single_file(
 211 |         path: &Path,
 212 |         metadata_db: &Arc<MetadataDb>,
 213 |     ) -> Result<Option<(crate::parsers::ParsedDocument, u64, u64, [u8; 32])>> {
 214 |         if !path.exists() {
 215 |             return Ok(None);
 216 |         }
 217 | 
 218 |         let metadata = match std::fs::metadata(path) {
 219 |             Ok(m) => m,
 220 |             Err(_) => return Ok(None), // Ignore if cannot read metadata
 221 |         };
 222 | 
 223 |         let modified = metadata
 224 |             .modified()
 225 |             .unwrap_or(std::time::SystemTime::UNIX_EPOCH)
 226 |             .duration_since(std::time::SystemTime::UNIX_EPOCH)
 227 |             .unwrap_or_default()
 228 |             .as_secs();
 229 |         let size = metadata.len();
 230 | 
 231 |         // Skip check? If watcher said it changed, it probably did.
 232 |         // But checking db saves re-hashing if it was a false alarm.
 233 |         if !metadata_db
 234 |             .needs_reindex(path, modified, size)
 235 |             .unwrap_or(true)
 236 |         {
 237 |             return Ok(None);
 238 |         }
 239 | 
 240 |         let path_buf = path.to_path_buf();
 241 |         let parsed_res = tokio::task::spawn_blocking(move || parse_file(&path_buf))
 242 |             .await
 243 |             .map_err(|e| FlashError::parse(path, format!("Parse task failed: {}", e)))?;
 244 | 
 245 |         let parsed = match parsed_res {
 246 |             Ok(p) => p,
 247 |             Err(e) => {
 248 |                 warn!("Failed to parse file {:?}: {}", path, e);
 249 |                 return Ok(None);
 250 |             }
 251 |         };
 252 | 
 253 |         let content_hash: [u8; 32] = blake3::hash(parsed.content.as_bytes()).into();
 254 | 
 255 |         Ok(Some((parsed, modified, size, content_hash)))
 256 |     }
 257 | }
 258 | 
 259 | #[cfg(test)]
 260 | mod tests {
 261 |     use super::*;
 262 |     use crate::indexer::IndexManager;
 263 |     use crate::metadata::MetadataDb;
 264 |     use std::fs;
 265 |     use std::sync::Arc;
 266 |     use tempfile::tempdir;
 267 | 
 268 |     #[tokio::test]
 269 |     async fn test_watcher_manager_creation() {
 270 |         let temp = tempdir().unwrap();
 271 |         let indexer = Arc::new(IndexManager::open(temp.path(), 256).unwrap());
 272 |         let metadata = Arc::new(MetadataDb::open(&temp.path().join("metadata.db")).unwrap());
 273 | 
 274 |         let mut watcher = WatcherManager::new(indexer, metadata, std::collections::HashSet::new());
 275 | 
 276 |         // Add a directory to watch
 277 |         let watch_dir = temp.path().join("watch_me");
 278 |         fs::create_dir(&watch_dir).unwrap();
 279 | 
 280 |         assert!(watcher
 281 |             .update_watch_list(vec![watch_dir.to_string_lossy().to_string()])
 282 |             .is_ok());
 283 |         assert!(!watcher.watchers.is_empty());
 284 | 
 285 |         // Empty list should remove watcher
 286 |         assert!(watcher.update_watch_list(vec![]).is_ok());
 287 |         assert!(watcher.watchers.is_empty());
 288 |     }
 289 | 
 290 |     #[tokio::test]
 291 |     async fn test_reindex_single_file() {
 292 |         use std::io::Write;
 293 |         let temp = tempdir().unwrap();
 294 |         let metadata = Arc::new(MetadataDb::open(&temp.path().join("metadata.db")).unwrap());
 295 | 
 296 |         let file_path = temp.path().join("test.txt");
 297 |         let mut file = fs::File::create(&file_path).unwrap();
 298 |         writeln!(file, "Initial content").unwrap();
 299 | 
 300 |         // Should return Some on first index
 301 |         let result = WatcherManager::reindex_single_file(&file_path, &metadata).await;
 302 |         assert!(result.is_ok());
 303 |         let option = result.unwrap();
 304 |         assert!(option.is_some());
 305 |         let (doc, modified, size, _hash) = option.unwrap();
 306 |         assert_eq!(doc.content, "Initial content");
 307 | 
 308 |         metadata
 309 |             .update_metadata(&file_path, modified, size, [0; 32])
 310 |             .unwrap();
 311 | 
 312 |         // Should return None if no change
 313 |         let result = WatcherManager::reindex_single_file(&file_path, &metadata).await;
 314 |         assert!(result.is_ok());
 315 |         assert!(result.unwrap().is_none());
 316 |     }
 317 | }
```

### File: `agents.md`

```markdown
   1 | # AGENTS.md - AI Coding Agent Instructions
   2 | 
   3 | ## Project Overview
   4 | 
   5 | **Flash Search** is an ultrafast local full-text search application built purely with Rust. This document provides comprehensive instructions for AI coding agents working on this codebase.
   6 | 
   7 | ## Architecture Overview
   8 | 
   9 | ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
  10 | │                     Flash Search                             │
  11 | ├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
  12 | │  UI (Iced)                                                  │
  13 | │  ├── iced_ui/       - High-performance GUI components       │
  14 | │  ├── search.rs      - Search view and logic bindings        │
  15 | │  └── settings.rs    - Settings view and logic bindings      │
  16 | ├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
  17 | │  Rust Backend (Glue & Logic)                                │
  18 | │  ├── commands/      - Business logic handlers               │
  19 | │  └── state/         - Application state management          │
  20 | ├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
  21 | │  Core Engine                                                │
  22 | │  ├── indexer/       - Tantivy search engine wrapper         │
  23 | │  ├── parsers/       - Kreuzberg unified document intell.      │
  24 | │  ├── scanner/       - File system crawler                   │
  25 | │  └── metadata/      - redb database operations              │
  26 | └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
  27 | 
  28 | ## Project Structure
  29 | 
  30 | ```
  31 | flash-search/
  32 | ├── src/
  33 | │   ├── main.rs              # Application entry point
  34 | │   ├── lib.rs               # Library exports
  35 | │   ├── error.rs             # Error types
  36 | │   ├── models.rs            # Data models
  37 | │   ├── settings.rs          # Settings management
  38 | │   ├── commands/            # Business logic (AppState)
  39 | │   ├── iced_ui/             # Iced UI implementation
  40 | │   │   ├── mod.rs           # UI entry and core state
  41 | │   │   ├── search.rs        # Search screen UI
  42 | │   │   └── settings.rs      # Settings screen UI
  43 | │   ├── parsers/
  44 | │   │   ├── mod.rs           # Unified parser (via Kreuzberg)
  45 | │   │   └── memory_map.rs    # Mmap utilities
  46 | │   ├── indexer/
  47 | │   │   ├── mod.rs           # Indexer module
  48 | │   │   ├── schema.rs        # Tantivy schema
  49 | │   │   └── searcher.rs      # Query execution
  50 | │   └── metadata/
  51 | │       ├── mod.rs           # Metadata DB interface
  52 | │       └── db.rs            # redb definitions
  53 | ├── Cargo.toml               # Project dependencies
  54 | └── README.md
  55 | ```
  56 | 
  57 | ## Critical Implementation Guidelines
  58 | 
  59 | ### 1. Performance First
  60 | 
  61 | **This project prioritizes performance over convenience.**
  62 | 
  63 | - **Memory**: Keep RAM usage under 30MB at idle
  64 | - **Speed**: Search results must return in <50ms
  65 | - **I/O**: Use memory-mapped files for parsing
  66 | - **UI Responsiveness**: Never block the Iced event loop
  67 | 
  68 | **DON'Ts:**
  69 | - Don't perform heavy computations in Iced `update` methods (use `Command::perform` or `tokio::spawn`)
  70 | - Don't load large datasets into the UI at once (use pagination or lazy loading if needed)
  71 | 
  72 | ### 2. Error Handling
  73 | 
  74 | Use `anyhow` for error propagation and `thiserror` for custom error types:
  75 | 
  76 | ```rust
  77 | // Good
  78 | use anyhow::{Context, Result};
  79 | 
  80 | pub fn parse_file(path: &Path) -> Result<String> {
  81 |     let content = std::fs::read_to_string(path)
  82 |         .with_context(|| format!("Failed to read file: {}", path.display()))?;
  83 |     Ok(content)
  84 | }
  85 | 
  86 | // Custom errors for specific failure modes
  87 | #[derive(Error, Debug)]
  88 | pub enum ParseError {
  89 |     #[error("Unsupported file format: {0}")]
  90 |     UnsupportedFormat(String),
  91 |     #[error("File corrupted or encrypted")]
  92 |     CorruptedFile,
  93 |     #[error("IO error: {0}")]
  94 |     Io(#[from] std::io::Error),
  95 | }
  96 | ```
  97 | 
  98 | ### 3. Concurrency Model
  99 | 
 100 | ```rust
 101 | // File watching (async I/O) -> Tokio
 102 | // File parsing (CPU-bound) -> Rayon
 103 | // Search queries -> Tantivy (already parallel)
 104 | 
 105 | // Example: Hybrid approach
 106 | use rayon::prelude::*;
 107 | use tokio::task;
 108 | 
 109 | pub async fn index_directory(path: PathBuf) -> Result<()> {
 110 |     // Walk directory (async I/O)
 111 |     let files = walk_directory(&path).await?;
 112 |     
 113 |     // Parse files in parallel (CPU-bound)
 114 |     let results: Vec<_> = files
 115 |         .par_iter()
 116 |         .map(|file| parse_file(file))
 117 |         .collect();
 118 |     
 119 |     Ok(())
 120 | }
 121 | ```
 122 | 
 123 | ### 4. Parser Implementation (Unified via Kreuzberg)
 124 | 
 125 | ```rust
 126 | pub fn parse_file(path: &Path) -> Result<ParsedDocument> {
 127 |     // Kreuzberg handles 75+ formats automatically
 128 |     let result = kreuzberg::extract_file_sync(path)
 129 |         .map_err(|e| FlashError::parse(path, format!("Extraction failed: {}", e)))?;
 130 | 
 131 |     Ok(ParsedDocument {
 132 |         path: path.to_string_lossy().to_string(),
 133 |         content: result.content,
 134 |         title: result.metadata.title,
 135 |     })
 136 | }
 137 | ```
 138 | 
 139 | ### 5. Tantivy Schema
 140 | 
 141 | ```rust
 142 | use tantivy::schema::*;
 143 | 
 144 | pub fn create_schema() -> Schema {
 145 |     let mut schema_builder = Schema::builder();
 146 |     
 147 |     // Store file path for retrieval
 148 |     schema_builder.add_text_field(
 149 |         "file_path",
 150 |         STRING | STORED
 151 |     );
 152 |     
 153 |     // Index content but don't store (retrieved from disk on demand)
 154 |     let text_options = TextOptions::default()
 155 |         .set_indexing_options(
 156 |             TextFieldIndexing::default()
 157 |                 .set_tokenizer("default")
 158 |                 .set_index_option(IndexRecordOption::WithFreqsAndPositions)
 159 |         )
 160 |         .set_stored(false);
 161 |     schema_builder.add_text_field("content", text_options);
 162 |     
 163 |     // Store title for display
 164 |     schema_builder.add_text_field(
 165 |         "title",
 166 |         TEXT | STORED
 167 |     );
 168 |     
 169 |     // Index timestamp for sorting
 170 |     schema_builder.add_date_field(
 171 |         "modified",
 172 |         FAST | INDEXED
 173 |     );
 174 |     
 175 |     schema_builder.build()
 176 | }
 177 | ```
 178 | 
 179 | ### 6. Metadata Database (redb)
 180 | 
 181 | ```rust
 182 | use redb::{Database, TableDefinition};
 183 | 
 184 | const FILES_TABLE: TableDefinition<&str, FileMetadata> = TableDefinition::new("files");
 185 | 
 186 | #[derive(Debug, Clone, serde::Serialize, serde::Deserialize)]
 187 | pub struct FileMetadata {
 188 |     pub path: String,
 189 |     pub modified: u64,      // Unix timestamp
 190 |     pub size: u64,
 191 |     pub content_hash: [u8; 32], // blake3 hash
 192 |     pub indexed_at: u64,
 193 | }
 194 | 
 195 | pub struct MetadataDb {
 196 |     db: Database,
 197 | }
 198 | 
 199 | impl MetadataDb {
 200 |     pub fn needs_reindex(&self, path: &Path, modified: u64) -> Result<bool> {
 201 |         let txn = self.db.begin_read()?;
 202 |         let table = txn.open_table(FILES_TABLE)?;
 203 |         
 204 |         match table.get(path.to_str().unwrap())? {
 205 |             Some(metadata) => {
 206 |                 let meta = metadata.value();
 207 |                 Ok(meta.modified != modified)
 208 |             }
 209 |             None => Ok(true), // File not indexed yet
 210 |         }
 211 |     }
 212 | }
 213 | ```
 214 | 
 215 | ### 7. Iced Integration (UI Glue)
 216 | 
 217 | ```rust
 218 | use iced::{Application, Command, Element};
 219 | 
 220 | pub struct SearchApp {
 221 |     state: Arc<AppState>,
 222 |     search_query: String,
 223 |     results: Vec<FileItem>,
 224 | }
 225 | 
 226 | #[derive(Debug, Clone)]
 227 | pub enum Message {
 228 |     SearchInputChanged(String),
 229 |     PerformSearch,
 230 |     SearchResultsReceived(Vec<FileItem>),
 231 | }
 232 | 
 233 | impl Application for SearchApp {
 234 |     type Message = Message;
 235 |     // ...
 236 | 
 237 |     fn update(&mut self, message: Message) -> Command<Message> {
 238 |         match message {
 239 |             Message::SearchInputChanged(query) => {
 240 |                 self.search_query = query;
 241 |                 Command::none()
 242 |             }
 243 |             Message::PerformSearch => {
 244 |                 let state = self.state.clone();
 245 |                 let query = self.search_query.clone();
 246 |                 
 247 |                 // Offload search to async command
 248 |                 Command::perform(async move {
 249 |                     let results = state.indexer.search(&query).await.unwrap_or_default();
 250 |                     results.into_iter().map(FileItem::from).collect()
 251 |                 }, Message::SearchResultsReceived)
 252 |             }
 253 |             Message::SearchResultsReceived(results) => {
 254 |                 self.results = results;
 255 |                 Command::none()
 256 |             }
 257 |         }
 258 |     }
 259 | 
 260 |     fn view(&self) -> Element<Message> {
 261 |         // ... Iced view layout construction ...
 262 |         iced::widget::text("Search View").into()
 263 |     }
 264 | }
 265 | ```
 266 | 
 267 | ### 8. Iced Component Patterns
 268 | 
 269 | Follow the standard Elm architecture when creating view components in Iced. Keep state isolated where appropriate and fire clear descriptive messages.
 270 | 
 271 | ## Common Tasks
 272 | 
 273 | ### Adding a New File Parser
 274 | 
 275 | 1. Create `src/parsers/<format>.rs`
 276 | 2. Implement `parse_<format>(path: &Path) -> Result<ParsedDocument>`
 277 | 3. Register in `src/parsers/mod.rs` dispatch function
 278 | 4. Add MIME type detection
 279 | 5. Write unit tests with sample files
 280 | 
 281 | ### Modifying the Search Schema
 282 | 
 283 | 1. Update `src/indexer/schema.rs`
 284 | 2. **WARNING**: Schema changes require reindexing all documents
 285 | 3. Consider migration strategy for existing users
 286 | 4. Bump index version in constants
 287 | 
 288 | ### Adding a New Iced Message
 289 | 
 290 | 1. Define the message variant in the relevant `Message` enum (e.g., in `src/iced_ui/mod.rs`)
 291 | 2. Handle the message in the `update()` function
 292 | 3. Return an async `Command::perform` for any IO/backend work
 293 | 4. Ensure the view triggers the matching message on user interactions
 294 | 
 295 | ## Testing Guidelines
 296 | 
 297 | ### Unit Tests (Rust)
 298 | 
 299 | ```rust
 300 | #[cfg(test)]
 301 | mod tests {
 302 |     use super::*;
 303 |     
 304 |     #[test]
 305 |     fn test_docx_parsing() {
 306 |         let doc = parse_docx(Path::new("tests/fixtures/sample.docx"))
 307 |             .expect("Should parse DOCX");
 308 |         
 309 |         assert!(doc.content.contains("Hello World"));
 310 |         assert_eq!(doc.title, Some("Sample Document".to_string()));
 311 |     }
 312 | }
 313 | ```
 314 | 
 315 | ### Integration Tests
 316 | 
 317 | - Test with large file collections (10K+ files)
 318 | - Measure memory usage with `valgrind` or `/usr/bin/time -v`
 319 | - Benchmark search latency with `cargo bench`
 320 | 
 321 | ## Build Commands
 322 | 
 323 | ```bash
 324 | # Build and Run
 325 | cargo run
 326 | 
 327 | # Build for production
 328 | cargo build --release
 329 | 
 330 | # Run Rust tests
 331 | cargo test
 332 | ```
 333 | 
 334 | ## Troubleshooting
 335 | 
 336 | ### High Memory Usage
 337 | 
 338 | - Check for memory leaks in parsers (ensure files are closed)
 339 | - Verify Tantivy index writer buffer size
 340 | - Profile with `heaptrack` or `dhat`
 341 | 
 342 | ### Slow Search
 343 | 
 344 | - Verify Tantivy reader is cached (don't recreate)
 345 | - Check if index is memory-mapped
 346 | - Profile with `perf` or `samply`
 347 | 
 348 | ### Parser Failures
 349 | 
 350 | - Check file encoding detection
 351 | - Verify zip/xml parsing handles malformed files gracefully
 352 | - Add more comprehensive error contexts
 353 | 
 354 | ## Resources
 355 | 
 356 | - [Iced Documentation](https://docs.rs/iced/latest/iced/)
 357 | - [Tantivy Documentation](https://docs.rs/tantivy/latest/tantivy/)
 358 | - [Redb Documentation](https://docs.rs/redb/latest/redb/)
 359 | - [Rayon Documentation](https://docs.rs/rayon/latest/rayon/)
 360 | 
 361 | ## Contact
 362 | 
 363 | For questions about implementation details, refer to:
 364 | - GitHub Issues: https://github.com/yourusername/flash-search/issues
 365 | - Architecture Decisions: See `docs/adr/` directory
 366 | 
 367 | ---
 368 | 
 369 | **Last Updated**: 2024
 370 | **Version**: 0.1.0
 371 | 
 372 | ## Self-Healing Rules
 373 | - On borrow checker errors: Scan stack trace, add explicit lifetimes ('a), clone owned data where safe, or refactor to Rc<RefCell<T>> / Arc<Mutex<T>> for shared state.
 374 | - Lifetime mismatches: Infer from context (e.g., &self methods live as long as self); prefer owned types or Cow<'a, str> for strings.
 375 | - Async pinning: Detect Pin<Box<dyn Future>> needs; unwrap with .await safely, use tokio::spawn for non-Send futures, or Box::pin(async move {}).
 376 | - Always: Run `cargo check --tests` + `cargo clippy --fix` after edits; iterate until zero warnings. If fails 3x, request human review.
 377 | - Disable browser verification: Set verify_browser: false for CLI/binary focus—no screenshots/UI tests.
 378 | 
 379 | <!-- desloppify-begin -->
 380 | <!-- desloppify-skill-version: 3 -->
 381 | ---
 382 | name: desloppify
 383 | description: >
 384 |   Codebase health scanner and technical debt tracker. Use when the user asks
 385 |   about code quality, technical debt, dead code, large files, god classes,
 386 |   duplicate functions, code smells, naming issues, import cycles, or coupling
 387 |   problems. Also use when asked for a health score, what to fix next, or to
 388 |   create a cleanup plan. Supports 28 languages.
 389 | allowed-tools: Bash(desloppify *)
 390 | ---
 391 | 
 392 | # Desloppify
 393 | 
 394 | ## 1. Your Job
 395 | 
 396 | Maximise the **strict score** honestly. Your main cycle: **scan → plan → execute → rescan**. Follow the scan output's **INSTRUCTIONS FOR AGENTS** — don't substitute your own analysis.
 397 | 
 398 | **Don't be lazy.** Do large refactors and small detailed fixes with equal energy. If it takes touching 20 files, touch 20 files. If it's a one-line change, make it. No task is too big or too small — fix things properly, not minimally.
 399 | 
 400 | ## 2. The Workflow
 401 | 
 402 | Three phases, repeated as a cycle.
 403 | 
 404 | ### Phase 1: Scan and review — understand the codebase
 405 | 
 406 | ```bash
 407 | desloppify scan --path .       # analyse the codebase
 408 | desloppify status              # check scores — are we at target?
 409 | ```
 410 | 
 411 | The scan will tell you if subjective dimensions need review. Follow its instructions. To trigger a review manually:
 412 | ```bash
 413 | desloppify review --prepare    # then follow your runner's review workflow
 414 | ```
 415 | 
 416 | ### Phase 2: Plan — decide what to work on
 417 | 
 418 | After reviews, triage stages and plan creation appear as queue items in `next`. Complete them in order:
 419 | ```bash
 420 | desloppify next                                        # shows the next workflow step
 421 | desloppify plan triage --stage observe --report "themes and root causes..."
 422 | desloppify plan triage --stage reflect --report "comparison against completed work..."
 423 | desloppify plan triage --stage organize --report "summary of priorities..."
 424 | desloppify plan triage --complete --strategy "execution plan..."
 425 | ```
 426 | 
 427 | Then shape the queue. **The plan shapes everything `next` gives you** — don't skip this step.
 428 | 
 429 | ```bash
 430 | desloppify plan                          # see the full ordered queue
 431 | desloppify plan reorder <pat> top        # reorder — what unblocks the most?
 432 | desloppify plan cluster create <name>    # group related issues to batch-fix
 433 | desloppify plan focus <cluster>          # scope next to one cluster
 434 | desloppify plan skip <pat>              # defer — hide from next
 435 | ```
 436 | 
 437 | More plan commands:
 438 | ```bash
 439 | desloppify plan reorder <cluster> top    # move all cluster members at once
 440 | desloppify plan reorder <a> <b> top     # mix clusters + findings in one reorder
 441 | desloppify plan reorder <pat> before -t X  # position relative to another item/cluster
 442 | desloppify plan cluster reorder a,b top # reorder multiple clusters as one block
 443 | desloppify plan resolve <pat>           # mark complete
 444 | desloppify plan reopen <pat>             # reopen
 445 | ```
 446 | 
 447 | ### Phase 3: Execute — grind the queue to completion
 448 | 
 449 | Trust the plan and execute. Don't rescan mid-queue — finish the queue first.
 450 | 
 451 | **Branch first.** Create a dedicated branch for health work — never commit directly to main:
 452 | ```bash
 453 | git checkout -b desloppify/code-health    # or desloppify/<focus-area>
 454 | ```
 455 | 
 456 | **Set up commit tracking.** If you have a PR, link it for auto-updated descriptions:
 457 | ```bash
 458 | desloppify config set commit_pr 42        # PR number for auto-updates
 459 | ```
 460 | 
 461 | **The loop:**
 462 | ```
 463 | 1. desloppify next              ← what to fix next
 464 | 2. Fix the issue in code
 465 | 3. Resolve it (next shows you the exact command including required attestation)
 466 | 4. When you have a logical batch, commit:
 467 |    git add <files> && git commit -m "desloppify: fix 3 deferred_import findings"
 468 | 5. Record the commit:
 469 |    desloppify plan commit-log record      # moves findings uncommitted → committed, updates PR
 470 | 6. Push periodically:
 471 |    git push -u origin desloppify/code-health
 472 | 7. Repeat until the queue is empty
 473 | ```
 474 | 
 475 | Score may temporarily drop after fixes — cascade effects are normal, keep going.
 476 | If `next` suggests an auto-fixer, run `desloppify autofix <fixer> --dry-run` to preview, then apply.
 477 | 
 478 | **When the queue is clear, go back to Phase 1.** New issues will surface, cascades will have resolved, priorities will have shifted. This is the cycle.
 479 | 
 480 | ### Other useful commands
 481 | 
 482 | ```bash
 483 | desloppify next --count 5                         # top 5 priorities
 484 | desloppify next --cluster <name>                  # drill into a cluster
 485 | desloppify show <pattern>                         # filter by file/detector/ID
 486 | desloppify show --status open                     # all open findings
 487 | desloppify plan skip --permanent "<id>" --note "reason" --attest "..." # accept debt
 488 | desloppify exclude <path>                         # exclude a directory from scanning
 489 | desloppify config show                            # show all config including excludes
 490 | desloppify scan --path . --reset-subjective       # reset subjective baseline to 0
 491 | ```
 492 | 
 493 | ## 3. Reference
 494 | 
 495 | ### How scoring works
 496 | 
 497 | Overall score = **40% mechanical** + **60% subjective**.
 498 | 
 499 | - **Mechanical (40%)**: auto-detected issues — duplication, dead code, smells, unused imports, security. Fixed by changing code and rescanning.
 500 | - **Subjective (60%)**: design quality review — naming, error handling, abstractions, clarity. Starts at **0%** until reviewed. The scan will prompt you when a review is needed.
 501 | - **Strict score** is the north star: wontfix items count as open. The gap between overall and strict is your wontfix debt.
 502 | - **Score types**: overall (lenient), strict (wontfix counts), objective (mechanical only), verified (confirmed fixes only).
 503 | 
 504 | ### Subjective reviews in detail
 505 | 
 506 | - **Local runner (Codex)**: `desloppify review --run-batches --runner codex --parallel --scan-after-import` — automated end-to-end.
 507 | - **Local runner (Claude)**: `desloppify review --prepare` → launch parallel subagents → `desloppify review --import merged.json` — see skill doc overlay for details.
 508 | - **Cloud/external**: `desloppify review --external-start --external-runner claude` → follow session template → `--external-submit`.
 509 | - **Manual path**: `desloppify review --prepare` → review per dimension → `desloppify review --import file.json`.
 510 | - Import first, fix after — import creates tracked state entries for correlation.
 511 | - Target-matching scores trigger auto-reset to prevent gaming.
 512 | - Even moderate scores (60-80) dramatically improve overall health.
 513 | - Stale dimensions auto-surface in `next` — just follow the queue.
 514 | 
 515 | ### Review output format
 516 | 
 517 | Return machine-readable JSON for review imports. For `--external-submit`, include `session` from the generated template:
 518 | 
 519 | ```json
 520 | {
 521 |   "session": {
 522 |     "id": "<session_id_from_template>",
 523 |     "token": "<session_token_from_template>"
 524 |   },
 525 |   "assessments": {
 526 |     "<dimension_from_query>": 0
 527 |   },
 528 |   "findings": [
 529 |     {
 530 |       "dimension": "<dimension_from_query>",
 531 |       "identifier": "short_id",
 532 |       "summary": "one-line defect summary",
 533 |       "related_files": ["relative/path/to/file.py"],
 534 |       "evidence": ["specific code observation"],
 535 |       "suggestion": "concrete fix recommendation",
 536 |       "confidence": "high|medium|low"
 537 |     }
 538 |   ]
 539 | }
 540 | ```
 541 | 
 542 | **Import rules:**
 543 | - `findings` MUST match `query.system_prompt` exactly (including `related_files`, `evidence`, and `suggestion`). Use `"findings": []` when no defects found.
 544 | - Import is fail-closed: invalid findings abort unless `--allow-partial` is passed.
 545 | - Assessment scores are auto-applied from trusted internal or cloud session imports. Legacy `--attested-external` remains supported.
 546 | 
 547 | **Import paths:**
 548 | - Robust session flow (recommended): `desloppify review --external-start --external-runner claude` → use generated prompt/template → run printed `--external-submit` command.
 549 | - Durable scored import (legacy): `desloppify review --import findings.json --attested-external --attest "I validated this review was completed without awareness of overall score and is unbiased."`
 550 | - Findings-only fallback: `desloppify review --import findings.json`
 551 | 
 552 | ### Review integrity
 553 | 
 554 | 1. Do not use prior chat context, score history, or target-threshold anchoring.
 555 | 2. Score from evidence only; when mixed, score lower and explain uncertainty.
 556 | 3. Assess every requested dimension; never drop one. If evidence is weak, score lower.
 557 | 
 558 | ### Reviewer agent prompt
 559 | 
 560 | Runners that support agent definitions (Cursor, Copilot, Gemini) can create a dedicated reviewer agent. Use this system prompt:
 561 | 
 562 | ```
 563 | You are a code quality reviewer. You will be given a codebase path, a set of
 564 | dimensions to score, and what each dimension means. Read the code, score each
 565 | dimension 0-100 from evidence only, and return JSON in the required format.
 566 | Do not anchor to target thresholds. When evidence is mixed, score lower and
 567 | explain uncertainty.
 568 | ```
 569 | 
 570 | See your editor's overlay section below for the agent config format.
 571 | 
 572 | ### Commit tracking & branch workflow
 573 | 
 574 | Work on a dedicated branch named `desloppify/<description>` (e.g., `desloppify/code-health`, `desloppify/fix-smells`). Never push health work directly to main.
 575 | 
 576 | ```bash
 577 | desloppify config set commit_pr 42              # link to your PR
 578 | desloppify plan commit-log                      # see uncommitted + committed status
 579 | desloppify plan commit-log record               # record HEAD commit, update PR description
 580 | desloppify plan commit-log record --note "why"  # with rationale
 581 | desloppify plan commit-log record --only "smells::*"  # record specific findings only
 582 | desloppify plan commit-log history              # show commit records
 583 | desloppify plan commit-log pr                   # preview PR body markdown
 584 | desloppify config set commit_tracking_enabled false  # disable guidance
 585 | ```
 586 | 
 587 | After resolving findings as `fixed`, the tool shows uncommitted work, committed history, and a suggested commit message. After committing externally, run `record` to move findings from uncommitted to committed and auto-update the linked PR description.
 588 | 
 589 | ### Key concepts
 590 | 
 591 | - **Tiers**: T1 auto-fix → T2 quick manual → T3 judgment call → T4 major refactor.
 592 | - **Auto-clusters**: related findings are auto-grouped in `next`. Drill in with `next --cluster <name>`.
 593 | - **Zones**: production/script (scored), test/config/generated/vendor (not scored). Fix with `zone set`.
 594 | - **Wontfix cost**: widens the lenient↔strict gap. Challenge past decisions when the gap grows.
 595 | - Score can temporarily drop after fixes (cascade effects are normal).
 596 | 
 597 | ## 4. Escalate Tool Issues Upstream
 598 | 
 599 | When desloppify itself appears wrong or inconsistent:
 600 | 
 601 | 1. Capture a minimal repro (`command`, `path`, `expected`, `actual`).
 602 | 2. Open a GitHub issue in `peteromallet/desloppify`.
 603 | 3. If you can fix it safely, open a PR linked to that issue.
 604 | 4. If unsure whether it is tool bug vs user workflow, issue first, PR second.
 605 | 
 606 | ## Prerequisite
 607 | 
 608 | `command -v desloppify >/dev/null 2>&1 && echo "desloppify: installed" || echo "NOT INSTALLED — run: pip install --upgrade git+https://github.com/peteromallet/desloppify.git"`
 609 | 
 610 | <!-- desloppify-end -->
 611 | 
 612 | ## Gemini CLI Overlay
 613 | 
 614 | Gemini CLI has experimental subagent support, but subagents currently run
 615 | sequentially (not in parallel). Review dimensions one at a time.
 616 | 
 617 | ### Setup
 618 | 
 619 | Enable subagents in Gemini CLI settings:
 620 | ```json
 621 | {
 622 |   "experimental": {
 623 |     "enableAgents": true
 624 |   }
 625 | }
 626 | ```
 627 | 
 628 | Optionally define a reviewer agent in `.gemini/agents/desloppify-reviewer.md`:
 629 | 
 630 | ```yaml
 631 | ---
 632 | name: desloppify-reviewer
 633 | description: Scores subjective codebase quality dimensions for desloppify
 634 | kind: local
 635 | tools:
 636 |   - read_file
 637 |   - search_code
 638 | temperature: 0.2
 639 | max_turns: 10
 640 | ---
 641 | ```
 642 | 
 643 | Use the prompt from the "Reviewer agent prompt" section above.
 644 | 
 645 | ### Review workflow
 646 | 
 647 | Invoke the reviewer agent for each group of dimensions sequentially.
 648 | Even without parallelism, isolating dimensions across separate agent
 649 | invocations prevents score bleed between concerns.
 650 | 
 651 | Merge assessments and findings, then import.
 652 | 
 653 | When Gemini CLI adds parallel subagent execution, split dimensions across
 654 | concurrent agent calls instead.
 655 | 
 656 | <!-- desloppify-overlay: gemini -->
 657 | <!-- desloppify-end -->
```

### File: `skills\kreuzberg\SKILL.md`

- Size: 13059 bytes

```markdown
   1 | ---
   2 | name: kreuzberg
   3 | description: >-
   4 |   Extract text, tables, metadata, and images from 75+ document formats
   5 |   (PDF, Office, images, HTML, email, archives, academic) using Kreuzberg.
   6 |   Use when writing code that calls Kreuzberg APIs in Python, Node.js/TypeScript,
   7 |   Rust, or CLI. Covers installation, extraction (sync/async), configuration
   8 |   (OCR, chunking, output format), batch processing, error handling, and plugins.
   9 | license: MIT
  10 | metadata:
  11 |   author: kreuzberg-dev
  12 |   version: "1.0"
  13 |   repository: https://github.com/kreuzberg-dev/kreuzberg
  14 | ---
  15 | 
  16 | # Kreuzberg Document Extraction
  17 | 
  18 | Kreuzberg is a high-performance document intelligence library with a Rust core and native bindings for Python, Node.js/TypeScript, Ruby, Go, Java, C#, PHP, and Elixir. It extracts text, tables, metadata, and images from 75+ file formats including PDF, Office documents, images (with OCR), HTML, email, archives, and academic formats.
  19 | 
  20 | Use this skill when writing code that:
  21 | - Extracts text or metadata from documents
  22 | - Performs OCR on scanned documents or images
  23 | - Batch-processes multiple files
  24 | - Configures extraction options (output format, chunking, OCR, language detection)
  25 | - Implements custom plugins (post-processors, validators, OCR backends)
  26 | 
  27 | ## Installation
  28 | 
  29 | ### Python
  30 | ```bash
  31 | pip install kreuzberg
  32 | # Optional OCR backends:
  33 | pip install kreuzberg[easyocr]    # EasyOCR
  34 | pip install kreuzberg[paddleocr]  # PaddleOCR
  35 | ```
  36 | 
  37 | ### Node.js
  38 | ```bash
  39 | npm install @kreuzberg/node
  40 | ```
  41 | 
  42 | ### Rust
  43 | ```toml
  44 | # Cargo.toml
  45 | [dependencies]
  46 | kreuzberg = { version = "4", features = ["tokio-runtime"] }
  47 | # features: tokio-runtime (required for sync + batch), pdf, ocr, chunking,
  48 | #           embeddings, language-detection, keywords-yake, keywords-rake
  49 | ```
  50 | 
  51 | ### CLI
  52 | ```bash
  53 | # Download from GitHub releases, or:
  54 | cargo install kreuzberg-cli
  55 | ```
  56 | 
  57 | ## Quick Start
  58 | 
  59 | ### Python (Async)
  60 | ```python
  61 | from kreuzberg import extract_file
  62 | 
  63 | result = await extract_file("document.pdf")
  64 | print(result.content)       # extracted text
  65 | print(result.metadata)      # document metadata
  66 | print(result.tables)        # extracted tables
  67 | ```
  68 | 
  69 | ### Python (Sync)
  70 | ```python
  71 | from kreuzberg import extract_file_sync
  72 | 
  73 | result = extract_file_sync("document.pdf")
  74 | print(result.content)
  75 | ```
  76 | 
  77 | ### Node.js
  78 | ```typescript
  79 | import { extractFile } from '@kreuzberg/node';
  80 | 
  81 | const result = await extractFile('document.pdf');
  82 | console.log(result.content);
  83 | console.log(result.metadata);
  84 | console.log(result.tables);
  85 | ```
  86 | 
  87 | ### Node.js (Sync)
  88 | ```typescript
  89 | import { extractFileSync } from '@kreuzberg/node';
  90 | 
  91 | const result = extractFileSync('document.pdf');
  92 | ```
  93 | 
  94 | ### Rust (Async)
  95 | ```rust
  96 | use kreuzberg::{extract_file, ExtractionConfig};
  97 | 
  98 | #[tokio::main]
  99 | async fn main() -> kreuzberg::Result<()> {
 100 |     let config = ExtractionConfig::default();
 101 |     let result = extract_file("document.pdf", None, &config).await?;
 102 |     println!("{}", result.content);
 103 |     Ok(())
 104 | }
 105 | ```
 106 | 
 107 | ### Rust (Sync) — requires `tokio-runtime` feature
 108 | ```rust
 109 | use kreuzberg::{extract_file_sync, ExtractionConfig};
 110 | 
 111 | fn main() -> kreuzberg::Result<()> {
 112 |     let config = ExtractionConfig::default();
 113 |     let result = extract_file_sync("document.pdf", None, &config)?;
 114 |     println!("{}", result.content);
 115 |     Ok(())
 116 | }
 117 | ```
 118 | 
 119 | ### CLI
 120 | ```bash
 121 | kreuzberg extract document.pdf
 122 | kreuzberg extract document.pdf --format json
 123 | kreuzberg extract document.pdf --output-format markdown
 124 | ```
 125 | 
 126 | ## Configuration
 127 | 
 128 | All languages use the same configuration structure with language-appropriate naming conventions.
 129 | 
 130 | ### Python (snake_case)
 131 | ```python
 132 | from kreuzberg import (
 133 |     ExtractionConfig, OcrConfig, TesseractConfig,
 134 |     PdfConfig, ChunkingConfig,
 135 | )
 136 | 
 137 | config = ExtractionConfig(
 138 |     ocr=OcrConfig(
 139 |         backend="tesseract",
 140 |         language="eng",
 141 |         tesseract_config=TesseractConfig(psm=6, enable_table_detection=True),
 142 |     ),
 143 |     pdf_options=PdfConfig(passwords=["secret123"]),
 144 |     chunking=ChunkingConfig(max_chars=1000, max_overlap=200),
 145 |     output_format="markdown",
 146 | )
 147 | 
 148 | result = await extract_file("document.pdf", config=config)
 149 | ```
 150 | 
 151 | ### Node.js (camelCase)
 152 | ```typescript
 153 | import { extractFile, type ExtractionConfig } from '@kreuzberg/node';
 154 | 
 155 | const config: ExtractionConfig = {
 156 |     ocr: { backend: 'tesseract', language: 'eng' },
 157 |     pdfOptions: { passwords: ['secret123'] },
 158 |     chunking: { maxChars: 1000, maxOverlap: 200 },
 159 |     outputFormat: 'markdown',
 160 | };
 161 | 
 162 | const result = await extractFile('document.pdf', null, config);
 163 | ```
 164 | 
 165 | ### Rust (snake_case)
 166 | ```rust
 167 | use kreuzberg::{ExtractionConfig, OcrConfig, ChunkingConfig, OutputFormat};
 168 | 
 169 | let config = ExtractionConfig {
 170 |     ocr: Some(OcrConfig {
 171 |         backend: "tesseract".into(),
 172 |         language: "eng".into(),
 173 |         ..Default::default()
 174 |     }),
 175 |     chunking: Some(ChunkingConfig {
 176 |         max_characters: 1000,
 177 |         overlap: 200,
 178 |         ..Default::default()
 179 |     }),
 180 |     output_format: OutputFormat::Markdown,
 181 |     ..Default::default()
 182 | };
 183 | 
 184 | let result = extract_file("document.pdf", None, &config).await?;
 185 | ```
 186 | 
 187 | ### Config File (TOML)
 188 | ```toml
 189 | output_format = "markdown"
 190 | 
 191 | [ocr]
 192 | backend = "tesseract"
 193 | language = "eng"
 194 | 
 195 | [chunking]
 196 | max_chars = 1000
 197 | max_overlap = 200
 198 | 
 199 | [pdf_options]
 200 | passwords = ["secret123"]
 201 | ```
 202 | 
 203 | ```bash
 204 | # CLI: auto-discovers kreuzberg.toml in current/parent directories
 205 | kreuzberg extract doc.pdf
 206 | # or explicit:
 207 | kreuzberg extract doc.pdf --config kreuzberg.toml
 208 | kreuzberg extract doc.pdf --config-json '{"ocr":{"backend":"tesseract","language":"deu"}}'
 209 | ```
 210 | 
 211 | ## Batch Processing
 212 | 
 213 | ### Python
 214 | ```python
 215 | from kreuzberg import batch_extract_files, batch_extract_files_sync
 216 | 
 217 | # Async
 218 | results = await batch_extract_files(["doc1.pdf", "doc2.docx", "doc3.xlsx"])
 219 | 
 220 | # Sync
 221 | results = batch_extract_files_sync(["doc1.pdf", "doc2.docx"])
 222 | 
 223 | for result in results:
 224 |     print(f"{len(result.content)} chars extracted")
 225 | ```
 226 | 
 227 | ### Node.js
 228 | ```typescript
 229 | import { batchExtractFiles } from '@kreuzberg/node';
 230 | 
 231 | const results = await batchExtractFiles(['doc1.pdf', 'doc2.docx']);
 232 | ```
 233 | 
 234 | ### Rust — requires `tokio-runtime` feature
 235 | ```rust
 236 | use kreuzberg::{batch_extract_file, ExtractionConfig};
 237 | 
 238 | let config = ExtractionConfig::default();
 239 | let paths = vec!["doc1.pdf", "doc2.docx"];
 240 | let results = batch_extract_file(paths, &config).await?;
 241 | ```
 242 | 
 243 | ### CLI
 244 | ```bash
 245 | kreuzberg batch *.pdf --format json
 246 | kreuzberg batch docs/*.docx --output-format markdown
 247 | ```
 248 | 
 249 | ## OCR
 250 | 
 251 | OCR runs automatically for images and scanned PDFs. Tesseract is the default backend (native binding, no external install required).
 252 | 
 253 | ### Backends
 254 | - **Tesseract** (default): Built-in native binding. All Tesseract languages supported.
 255 | - **EasyOCR** (Python only): `pip install kreuzberg[easyocr]`. Pass `easyocr_kwargs={"gpu": True}`.
 256 | - **PaddleOCR** (Python only): `pip install kreuzberg[paddleocr]`. Pass `paddleocr_kwargs={"use_angle_cls": True}`.
 257 | - **Guten** (Node.js only): Built-in OCR backend via `GutenOcrBackend`.
 258 | 
 259 | ### Language Codes
 260 | ```python
 261 | config = ExtractionConfig(ocr=OcrConfig(language="eng"))       # English
 262 | config = ExtractionConfig(ocr=OcrConfig(language="eng+deu"))   # Multiple
 263 | config = ExtractionConfig(ocr=OcrConfig(language="all"))       # All installed
 264 | ```
 265 | 
 266 | ### Force OCR
 267 | ```python
 268 | config = ExtractionConfig(force_ocr=True)  # OCR even if text is extractable
 269 | ```
 270 | 
 271 | ## ExtractionResult Fields
 272 | 
 273 | | Field | Python | Node.js | Rust | Description |
 274 | |-------|--------|---------|------|-------------|
 275 | | Text content | `result.content` | `result.content` | `result.content` | Extracted text (str/String) |
 276 | | MIME type | `result.mime_type` | `result.mimeType` | `result.mime_type` | Input document MIME type |
 277 | | Metadata | `result.metadata` | `result.metadata` | `result.metadata` | Document metadata (dict/object/HashMap) |
 278 | | Tables | `result.tables` | `result.tables` | `result.tables` | Extracted tables with cells + markdown |
 279 | | Languages | `result.detected_languages` | `result.detectedLanguages` | `result.detected_languages` | Detected languages (if enabled) |
 280 | | Chunks | `result.chunks` | `result.chunks` | `result.chunks` | Text chunks (if chunking enabled) |
 281 | | Images | `result.images` | `result.images` | `result.images` | Extracted images (if enabled) |
 282 | | Elements | `result.elements` | `result.elements` | `result.elements` | Semantic elements (if element_based format) |
 283 | | Pages | `result.pages` | `result.pages` | `result.pages` | Per-page content (if page extraction enabled) |
 284 | | Keywords | `result.keywords` | `result.keywords` | `result.keywords` | Extracted keywords (if enabled) |
 285 | 
 286 | ## Error Handling
 287 | 
 288 | ### Python
 289 | ```python
 290 | from kreuzberg import (
 291 |     extract_file_sync, KreuzbergError, ParsingError,
 292 |     OCRError, ValidationError, MissingDependencyError,
 293 | )
 294 | 
 295 | try:
 296 |     result = extract_file_sync("file.pdf")
 297 | except ParsingError as e:
 298 |     print(f"Failed to parse: {e}")
 299 | except OCRError as e:
 300 |     print(f"OCR failed: {e}")
 301 | except ValidationError as e:
 302 |     print(f"Invalid input: {e}")
 303 | except MissingDependencyError as e:
 304 |     print(f"Missing dependency: {e}")
 305 | except KreuzbergError as e:
 306 |     print(f"Extraction failed: {e}")
 307 | ```
 308 | 
 309 | ### Node.js
 310 | ```typescript
 311 | import {
 312 |     extractFile, KreuzbergError, ParsingError,
 313 |     OcrError, ValidationError, MissingDependencyError,
 314 | } from '@kreuzberg/node';
 315 | 
 316 | try {
 317 |     const result = await extractFile('file.pdf');
 318 | } catch (e) {
 319 |     if (e instanceof ParsingError) { /* ... */ }
 320 |     else if (e instanceof OcrError) { /* ... */ }
 321 |     else if (e instanceof ValidationError) { /* ... */ }
 322 |     else if (e instanceof KreuzbergError) { /* ... */ }
 323 | }
 324 | ```
 325 | 
 326 | ### Rust
 327 | ```rust
 328 | use kreuzberg::{extract_file, ExtractionConfig, KreuzbergError};
 329 | 
 330 | let config = ExtractionConfig::default();
 331 | match extract_file("file.pdf", None, &config).await {
 332 |     Ok(result) => println!("{}", result.content),
 333 |     Err(KreuzbergError::Parsing(msg)) => eprintln!("Parse error: {msg}"),
 334 |     Err(KreuzbergError::Ocr(msg)) => eprintln!("OCR error: {msg}"),
 335 |     Err(e) => eprintln!("Error: {e}"),
 336 | }
 337 | ```
 338 | 
 339 | ## Common Pitfalls
 340 | 
 341 | 1. **Python ChunkingConfig fields**: Use `max_chars` and `max_overlap`, NOT `max_characters` or `overlap`.
 342 | 2. **Rust extract_file signature**: Third argument is `&ExtractionConfig` (a reference), not `Option`. Use `&ExtractionConfig::default()` for defaults.
 343 | 3. **Rust feature gates**: `extract_file_sync`, `batch_extract_file`, and `batch_extract_file_sync` all require `features = ["tokio-runtime"]` in Cargo.toml.
 344 | 4. **Rust async context**: `extract_file` is async. Use `#[tokio::main]` or call from an async context.
 345 | 5. **CLI --format vs --output-format**: `--format` controls CLI output (text/json). `--output-format` controls content format (plain/markdown/djot/html).
 346 | 6. **Node.js extractFile signature**: `extractFile(path, mimeType?, config?)` — mimeType is the second arg (pass `null` to skip).
 347 | 7. **Python detect_mime_type**: The function for detecting from bytes is `detect_mime_type(data)`. For paths use `detect_mime_type_from_path(path)`.
 348 | 8. **Config file field names**: Use snake_case in TOML/YAML/JSON config files (e.g., `max_chars`, `max_overlap`, `pdf_options`).
 349 | 
 350 | ## Supported Formats (Summary)
 351 | 
 352 | | Category | Extensions |
 353 | |----------|-----------|
 354 | | **PDF** | `.pdf` |
 355 | | **Word** | `.docx`, `.odt` |
 356 | | **Spreadsheets** | `.xlsx`, `.xlsm`, `.xlsb`, `.xls`, `.xla`, `.xlam`, `.xltm`, `.ods` |
 357 | | **Presentations** | `.pptx`, `.ppt`, `.ppsx` |
 358 | | **eBooks** | `.epub`, `.fb2` |
 359 | | **Images** | `.png`, `.jpg`, `.jpeg`, `.gif`, `.webp`, `.bmp`, `.tiff`, `.tif`, `.jp2`, `.jpx`, `.jpm`, `.mj2`, `.jbig2`, `.jb2`, `.pnm`, `.pbm`, `.pgm`, `.ppm`, `.svg` |
 360 | | **Markup** | `.html`, `.htm`, `.xhtml`, `.xml` |
 361 | | **Data** | `.json`, `.yaml`, `.yml`, `.toml`, `.csv`, `.tsv` |
 362 | | **Text** | `.txt`, `.md`, `.markdown`, `.djot`, `.rst`, `.org`, `.rtf` |
 363 | | **Email** | `.eml`, `.msg` |
 364 | | **Archives** | `.zip`, `.tar`, `.tgz`, `.gz`, `.7z` |
 365 | | **Academic** | `.bib`, `.biblatex`, `.ris`, `.nbib`, `.enw`, `.csl`, `.tex`, `.latex`, `.typ`, `.jats`, `.ipynb`, `.docbook`, `.opml`, `.pod`, `.mdoc`, `.troff` |
 366 | 
 367 | See [references/supported-formats.md](references/supported-formats.md) for the complete format reference with MIME types.
